COMPLIANCE & LEGAL FRAMEWORK** 10.1 Overview: Zero Trust Architecture
Trust\' Architecture, meaning the system does not trust itself, users, or external APIs
unless explicitly verified.
10.2 A. Multi-Tenancy Isolation (Row-Level Security) The Loophole: A hacker changing
their client
ID in a
request to see another company\'s data. The Fix: Postgres Row-Level Security (RLS)
ensures that every database
query is filtered by the authenticated user\'s identity. \-- Applied to ALL tables
containing client data ALTER
TABLE tickets ENABLE ROW LEVEL SECURITY; \-- Policy: Users can only see rows where their
ID matches
client_id CREATE POLICY client_isolation ON tickets FOR ALL USING (auth.uid() =
client_id); \-- auth.uid()
comes from JWT token, not request body What this prevents: - Broken Object Level
Authorization: A Client A
user cannot query SELECT \* FROM tickets WHERE client_id = 999 to view Client B\'s -
Horizontal Escalation:
Even if SQL injection occurs, the policy restricts data access. 10.3 B. Webhook Security
(HMAC Verification)
The Loophole: Anyone can fake a Shopify/Stripe order update by sending a JSON to your
webhook URL. The
Fix: We verify a cryptographic signature (HMAC) for every incoming webhook payload.
import hmac, hashlib

=== PAGE 91 ===
def verify_shopify_webhook(payload: bytes, signature: str, secret: str) -\> bool:
expected =
hmac.new(secret.encode(), payload, hashlib.sha256).hexdigest() return
hmac.compare_digest(expected,
signature) \# Constant-time compare 10.4 C. Data Retention & GDPR Compliance The Fix: A
\'3-Tiered\' Data
Retention Strategy that satisfies both operational needs and GDPR compliance.
Immediate soft-delete from Phone, Address closure active tables Anonymized Transaction
Logs: 5 years Hash PII
fields before (Cold) Timestamp, Amount, (Financial archiving Outcome audit) Audit Trail
Immutable action 5
GDPR \'Right to be Forgotten\' Endpoint: \@app.post(\'/api/account/delete\') async def
delete_account(user: User
= Depends(get_current_user)): # Delete user via application auth layer
db.execute("DELETE FROM users WHERE id = :user_id", {"user_id": user.id}) \# Step 1: Delete
from Auth
db.execute(\"UPDATE tickets SET status=\'deleted_archived\', user_id=NULL WHERE
client_id=?\",
user.client_id) return {\"message\": \"All PII deleted. Anonymized logs retained for 5
years per compliance.\"}

trivyaReviewTime_Minutes = 0.166; // PARWA: 10 seconds/ticket const totalTicketsPerMonth = dailyTickets \* 30; const

trivyaReviewTime_Minutes) / 60); const dollarValueOfTime = timeSaved_Hours \* (monthlyLaborCost / 173); Calculation D:

Auto-Response A. Metrics We Track: - Confidence Drift: Average Confidence Score per Client/Model. Trigger: If average

\'Approved\'). Trigger: If approval rate drops below 90% for 3 - Error Clustering: Types of errors occurring. Trigger: If the

truth** **THE PROBLEM:** System blindly approved AI \'recommendations\' because
confidence was 95%+
without considering edge cases where high confidence can still be wrong (e.g.,
fraudulent patterns that closely
mimic legitimate ones). The Fix: Confidence Score Transparency + Mandatory Override
Triggers Confidence
scores are now explicitly labeled as \'AI Confidence\' not \'Decision Quality.\' The UI
shows a breakdown of
WHY the confidence is high, not just the number itself. Hard-Coded Override Triggers
(regardless of confidence
detected in message \'address_country_change\', \# Account security concern
\'multiple_same_day_requests\' \#
Note: This is based on pattern matching, not a guarantee. Final decision is always
yours.\' **Issue 2: Blockchain
immutability** **THE PROBLEM:** Audit logs stored in a standard DB can be modified by a
DBA or hacker,
making them useless as legal evidence. Original approach of \'blockchain hashing\' was
vague and
unimplemented. The Fix: Immutable PostgreSQL Trigger + Hash Chain Every audit log entry
is chained to the
previous one using a SHA-256 hash, creating a tamper-evident ledger. A PostgreSQL
trigger prevents any
UPDATE or DELETE on audit_trail table. CREATE TABLE audit_trail ( id SERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
action
VARCHAR NOT NULL, actor_email VARCHAR NOT NULL, timestamp TIMESTAMPTZ DEFAULT
NOW(), payload JSONB, previous_hash VARCHAR(64), current_hash VARCHAR(64) GENERATED
ALWAYS AS ( encode(sha256((id::text \|\| action \|\| timestamp::text \|\|
previous_hash)::bytea), \'hex\') )
STORED ); CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION prevent_audit_modification() > RETURNS TRIGGER AS
\$\$ BEGIN RAISE EXCEPTION \'Audit trail is immutable. Modifications are prohibited.\';
END; \$\$
LANGUAGE plpgsql; CREATE TRIGGER audit_immutable BEFORE UPDATE OR DELETE ON audit_trail

=== PAGE 100 ===
Hardcoded threshold can be gamed **THE PROBLEM:** A fixed \'\$50 auto-approve limit\'
means a
sophisticated bad actor could split a \$200 fraudulent refund into 4 x \$49 requests,
all auto-approved. The Fix:
Velocity-Based Fraud Detection + Cumulative Limits def check_fraud_velocity(customer_id:
int, new_amount:
float) -\> dict: \# 1. Check cumulative refunds in rolling 30-day window
thirty_day_total = db.query( \'SELECT
SUM(amount) FROM refunds WHERE customer_id=? AND created_at > \> NOW()-INTERVAL 30
DAY\',
\'SELECT COUNT(\*) FROM refunds WHERE customer_id=? AND DATE(created_at)=TODAY()\',
new_amount) \> 150: return {\'action\': \'BLOCK\', \'reason\':
\'cumulative_limit_exceeded\'} if same_day_count
\>= 3: return {\'action\': \'BLOCK\', \'reason\': \'velocity_fraud_detected\'} return
{\'action\': \'ALLOW\'}
AI gives a customer incorrect medical, legal, or financial advice, PARWA could be held
liable. Original docs had
no clear liability framework. The Fix: Mandatory Disclaimer System + Knowledge Boundary
Detection Every AI
response is scanned for high-risk topic categories. If detected, a mandatory disclaimer
is appended: >
HIGH_RISK_TOPIC_PATTERNS = { \'medical\': \[\'medication\', \'dosage\', \'symptoms\',
\'diagnosis\'\],
\'legal\': \[\'lawsuit\', \'contract\', \'liability\', \'warranty\'\], \'financial\':
\[\'investment\', \'tax\', \'accounting\'\] } def
append_disclaimer_if_needed(response: str, topic: str) -\> str: disclaimers = {
\'medical\': \'\\n\\n\[Disclaimer:
This is general info, not medical advice. Consult a doctor.\]\', \'legal\':
\'\\n\\n\[Disclaimer: This is not legal advice.
Please consult a licensed attorney.\]\', \'financial\': \'\\n\\n\[Disclaimer: This is
not financial advice. Consult a
financial advisor.\]\' } if topic in disclaimers: return response + disclaimers\[topic\]
return response Terms of
Service Update: Added explicit clause: \'AI recommendations are advisory only. Client
bears final decision

PROBLEM:** If Shopify API goes down during a critical refund workflow, the AI would fail
silently or give
wrong information to the customer. The Fix: Circuit Breaker Pattern + Trust Preservation
Messages from
circuitbreaker import circuit \@circuit(failure_threshold=5, recovery_timeout=30) def
call_shopify_api(order_id:
str) -\> dict: response = requests.get(f\'https://shopify.com/api/orders/{order_id}\',
timeout=5)
response.raise_for_status() return response.json() def get_order_with_fallback(order_id:
str): try: return
call_shopify_api(order_id) except Exception: \# Fallback to cached data cached =
redis.get(f\'order:{order_id}\')
if cached: return json.loads(cached) \# Customer-facing trust message return
{\'status\': \'trust_message\',
\'customer_message\': \'Our systems are processing high volume. Check back in 5 min.\',
\'manager_alert\':
already-sent emails**
**THE PROBLEM:** The \'Recall\' command in Jarvis was described as being able to undo
sent emails. Emails
cannot be recalled once sent. This created false expectation. The Fix: Time-Gate + Pre-
Send Buffer System
Emails now have a 90-second pre-send buffer (configurable): def
schedule_email(email_data: dict,
delay_seconds: int = 90): job = scheduler.schedule( send_email, args=\[email_data\],
delay=delay_seconds,

TECHNIQUES** Technique 1: Agent Lightning (Proprietary) **What It Is:** PARWA\'s continuous learning loop that
automatically retrains the AI model weekly based on human corrections, making the AI smarter deployment. Agent
Lightning turns every Manager rejection into a training signal, creating a self-improving system. Fine-Tuning: Agent
Lightning script loads the base model (Llama-3-8B), trains on mistake pairs using PyTorch
85% 94% Manager Review Time 5 min/ticket 2.5 min/ticket 1.1 min/ticket Repeat Mistakes
23% 12% 3% Model
Framework: PyTorch Lightning (training orchestration). - Optimizer: Unsloth (2x--5x
faster fine-tuning on
consumer GPUs). - Base Model: Llama-3-8B (fits on T4 GPU, \~\$50/mo on RunPod). - Data
Format: JSONL
(prompt/completion pairs from mistake log). Technique 2: Custom GSD State Engine
(Proprietary) **What It
Is:** A structured state management system that replaces raw chat history with a

reducing token usage by 98% and eliminating hallucinations. Why We Use It: Standard LLMs

score += 2 if ticket\[\'customer_tier\'\]
== \'VIP\' else 0 score += 2 if ticket.get(\'amount\', 0) \> 100 else 0 score += 2 if

\'angry\' else 0 score += 4 if ticket.get(\'involves_legal\') else 0 score += 1 if
len(ticket\[\'message\'\].split()) \> 100
else 0 return score def route_to_model(score: int) -\> str: if score \<= 4: return

5: Batch Approval Intelligence (Proprietary) **What It Is:** Semantic clustering
algorithm that groups similar
approval requests together, reducing manager review time by 80% through intelligent
batching. The Clustering
Algorithm: from sklearn.metrics.pairwise import cosine_similarity import numpy as np def
cluster_approval_requests(pending_tickets: list) -\> list\[list\]: \# Step 1: Generate
embeddings for each ticket

=== PAGE 107 ===
embeddings = \[embed_text(t\[\'summary\'\]) for t in pending_tickets\] \# Step 2:
Calculate similarity matrix
similarity_matrix = cosine_similarity(embeddings) \# Step 3: Group tickets with \>85%
similarity batches = \[\]
visited = set() for i, ticket in enumerate(pending_tickets): if i not in visited: batch
= \[ticket\] for j in range(i+1,
len(pending_tickets)): if j not in visited and similarity_matrix\[i\]\[j\] \> 0.85:
batch.append(pending_tickets\[j\])
visited.add(j) batches.append(batch) return batches **CATEGORY 2: REASONING FRAMEWORKS**
Technique 6: Chain-of-Thought (CoT) Prompting **What It Is:** A prompting technique where the AI is instructed to show
its reasoning step-by-step before giving a final answer, dramatically improving accuracy on complex tasks. Standard vs. CoT
Prompt for Refund Decision: Standard (Bad): **Prompt:** Customer wants a
**Prompt:** A customer is requesting a refund. Think through this step-by-step: 1. Is
the order within the return
window? 2. Is the item eligible for return? 3. Are there any fraud signals? 4. What is
the customer\'s tier and
history? 5. Based on all factors, what is your recommendation and confidence? Show all
reasoning. Performance
Interpretation Fraud Detection 71% 89% Complex Edge Cases 54% 82%
**What It Is:** An advanced reasoning framework where the AI explores multiple reasoning
paths
simultaneously (like a decision tree), then selects the best path based on evaluation.
When PARWA Uses ToT: Complex fraud scenarios with ambiguous signals. - Policy exceptions
where multiple rules conflict. - VIP
customer decisions where relationship vs policy must be balanced. ToT Prompt Template
for Ambiguous Refund:
**Prompt:** Consider this refund request from three different perspectives
simultaneously. Path A (Policy
Enforcer): Strictly apply the 30-day return policy\... Path B (Customer Advocate):
Consider this is a VIP customer
with \$8,000 LTV\... Path C (Fraud Analyst): Review the velocity pattern and address
history\... After exploring
all three
paths, synthesize the best decision with confidence score. Performance vs CoT:
Is:** A framework where the AI alternates between reasoning steps and action steps,
allowing it to query external
systems (Shopify, Stripe) mid-reasoning to gather evidence before making a decision.
ReAct Flow for Refund
Decision: - THOUGHT: I need to check if the order is within the 30-day return window. -
ACTION:
query_shopify(order_id=\'8921\', fields=\[\'created_at\', \'fulfillment_status\'\]) -
OBSERVATION: Order created
12 days ago, fulfilled 10 days ago. Within window. - THOUGHT: I need to check if the
item is returnable. ACTION: check_return_policy(product_id=\'SKU-882\',
reason=\'wrong_size\') - OBSERVATION: Item is
returnable. Clothing items excluded from final sale policy. - THOUGHT: I need to check
customer fraud history.
- ACTION: check_customer_history(customer_id=\'C8291\') - OBSERVATION: 3-year account,
47 orders, 0
previous refunds, no fraud flags. - FINAL DECISION: APPROVE. Confidence: 94%. All checks
passed. Why
ReAct Beats Standard Prompting: Standard prompting relies on what the AI \'knows\' from
training data. ReAct
queries real-time data from actual systems, making decisions based on facts not
assumptions. Technique 9:

=== PAGE 108 ===
Reverse Thinking Prompting **What It Is:** Instead of asking \'What\'s the best
decision?\', we ask \'What would
make this the WRONG decision?\' This identifies hidden risks that forward-thinking
misses.
Reverse Thinking Prompt Template: **Prompt:** I\'m about to approve a \$75 refund for
customer C8291.
Before I do: List every reason this approval could be the WRONG decision. Consider:
fraud patterns, policy
violations, precedent-setting risks, financial impact, and any signals I might have
missed. Rate each risk from
1-10. Example Output: - Risk 1 (3/10): Customer has 3 refunds in 6 months. Pattern, but
all were legitimate. Low
high-value threshold. **AI Conclusion:** Primary risk is timing (28-day window). Request
additional evidence
(photo of damage). Otherwise approve. Adjusted Confidence: 88% -> 81% (reflecting timing
concern).
Technique 10: Universe-of-Thought (UoT) Prompting **What It Is:** An advanced framework
where
the AI
considers not just the current case but the entire universe of similar cases to identify
patterns, precedents, and
systemic issues. UoT Prompt Template: **Prompt:** Looking at this refund request in the
context of ALL similar
requests: How many similar requests have there been? What was the outcome pattern? Is
there a systemic issue
(bad product batch, supplier problem)? What precedent does this decision set? Should we
update our policy based
on this pattern? Example UoT Output: - Pattern Found: 23 similar \'wrong size\' returns
in last 7 days (vs 2 per
week normal). Anomaly: 500% spike. - Root Cause Hypothesis: New summer collection may
have sizing
SKU-442 for quality review. - Policy Update Suggested: Temporarily waive return shipping
for SKU-442 until
sizing issue resolved. Technique 11: Graph-of-Thought (GoT/GST) Prompting **What It
Is:** The most
branch can feed into another, creating non-linear, highly accurate analysis. When PARWA Uses GoT: Enterprise VIP cases
where multiple complex factors intersect. - Legal or compliance scenarios requiring
multi-domain expertise. - Strategic business decisions (churn prevention, contract
negotiations). GoT Structure
for Complex VIP Fraud Case: Node A (Customer History) -> feeds into -> Node C (Risk
Score)
Node B (Fraud Signals) -> feeds into -> Node C (Risk Score) Node C (Risk Score) -> feeds
into -> Node E
(Final Decision) Node D (Business Value) -> feeds into -> Node E (Final Decision) Node E
(Final Decision) ->
generates -> Node F (Action Plan) **CATEGORY 3: RAG (RETRIEVAL AUGMENTED GENERATION)
TECHNIQUES** Technique 12: CLARA Framework (Proprietary RAG) **What It Is:** PARWA\'s
custom
(Base): Standard vector similarity search against pgvector knowledge base. Finds
semantically similar content
searches for documents similar to that ideal answer. Finds better matches by searching
for what the answer
original question, retrieves results for all 3, deduplicates, then synthesizes. Catches
cases where different phrasing
isn\'t found, \'steps back\' to ask a more general question. Example: \'Can I return
shoes?\' steps back to \'What is

=== PAGE 109 ===
the general return policy?\' to find the answer in a broader context. Performance
Comparison:
(baseline) \+ HyDE 74% 1.8s 3,100 tokens \+ Multi-Query 81% 2.1s 4,200 tokens \+
Contextual 88% 1.4s 1,800
tokens Compression CLARA (All Layers) 91% 1.6s 2,100 tokens
Embeddings (HyDE)
**What It Is:** Instead of searching for documents similar to the question, generate a
hypothetical \'ideal answer\'
first, then search for documents similar to that ideal answer. Standard RAG vs HyDE:
Standard RAG:
**Query:** \'Can I return a gift card?\' -> Search vector DB for documents similar to
\'gift card return\' ->
\'non-returnable gift card policy section\' -> Returns: \'Excluded items from returns:
Electronics, Gift Cards, Final
Sale\...\' (CORRECT) Technique 14: Multi-Query RAG **What It Is:** Generate multiple
variations of the
original query, retrieve results for each, then synthesize. Catches cases where
different question phrasings retrieve
different relevant documents. Implementation: def
multi_query_retrieve(original_question: str, k: int = 5) -\> list:
\# Step 1: Generate 3 query variations using LLM variations = llm.generate( f\'Generate
3 different ways to ask:
\"{original_question}\". Return as JSON array.\' ) \# Step 2: Retrieve for each
variation all_docs = \[\] for query in
\[original_question\] + variations: docs = vectordb.similarity_search(query, k=k)
all_docs.extend(docs) \# Step 3:
Deduplicate by document ID unique_docs = {doc.id: doc for doc in all_docs}.values() \#
Step 4: Re-rank by
relevance to original question return rerank_by_relevance(list(unique_docs),
original_question) Technique 15:
Contextual Compression **What It Is:** After retrieving relevant documents, extract ONLY
the sentences that
Matters: A retrieved document about \'Return Policy\' contains: Introduction paragraph
(irrelevant), Eligible items
section (partially relevant), 30-day window paragraph (relevant), Exclusions list
(relevant), FAQ section
90% token reduction. Implementation: def compress_context(documents: list, question:
str) -\> str: compressed =
\[\] for doc in documents: \# Use small fast model to extract relevant sentences
relevant_sentences = fast_llm.extract( f\'From this document, extract ONLY sentences
that answer:
\"{question}\". Document: {doc.content}\' ) if relevant_sentences:
compressed.append(relevant_sentences) return
\' \'.join(compressed) Technique 16: Step-Back Prompting **What It Is:** When the AI
can\'t find a specific
answer, \'step back\' to a more general question to find the answer in a broader
context. Step-Back Chain
Example: - Original: \'Can I return the blue suede Chelsea boots from the Spring 2024
collection?\' -> No exact
match found. - Step Back 1: \'Can I return boots?\' -> Partial match: \'Footwear returns
accepted within 30 days.\'
- Step Back 2: \'What is the return policy for shoes?\' -> Full match: Complete footwear
return policy found. Step Back 3 (if needed): \'What is the general return policy?\' ->
Fallback to general policy. **CATEGORY 4:

=== PAGE 110 ===
MEMORY MANAGEMENT TECHNIQUES** Technique 17: Thread-of-Thought (ThoT) **What It Is:** A
memory technique that maintains a \'thread\' of the conversation\'s key insights across
a long interaction,
preventing the AI from losing context or contradicting earlier statements. The ThoT
Record (What We Track Per
Conversation): > THREAD_RECORD = { \'key_facts_established\': \[ \'Customer verified:
John Doe, Account
#C8291\', \'Issue: Refund for order #8921 (\$75)\', \'Root cause: Wrong size received\'
\], \'commitments_made\':
\[ \'Agent promised resolution within 24 hours\' \], \'customer_stated_preferences\':
\[\'Prefers email updates\'\],
\'escalation_history\': \[\], \'sentiment_arc\': \[\'neutral\', \'frustrated\',
\'calmer\'\] } Purpose: Before each AI
sending full chat history. Technique 18: Cognitive Reframing Protocol (CRP) **What It
Is:** A
token-compression technique that replaces raw conversation history with semantically
equivalent but much
Example:
they\'re the wrong size. User: I ordered size 10 but got size 8. User: Can I return
them? Agent: Of course! I\'ll
check your order. Agent: Order #8921 found. Agent: Yes, you\'re within our 30-day
window. Agent: What size do
Size exchange. ORDER: #8921. RECEIVED: Size 8. WANTED: Size 10. POLICY: Within 30-day
window.
STATUS: Awaiting approval. NEXT: Arrange exchange shipment. Token savings: 85 tokens vs
850 tokens =
90% reduction. Meaning preserved: 100%. Technique 19: Dynamic Context Window Management
**What It
Is:** Intelligent allocation of the model\'s context window across different types of
information, ensuring the
most critical information is always within the context window. Context Window Allocation
Strategy:
Dynamic Reallocation: When context pressure increases (long conversation), system automatically: Compresses older
conversation turns using CRP, Reduces RAG document length using Contextual Compression, Maintains CRITICAL sections at
full size always.
**CATEGORY 5: SELF-IMPROVEMENT TECHNIQUES** Technique 20: Self-Consistency Prompting
**What It Is:** Generate multiple independent answers to the same question using
different reasoning paths, then
select the answer that appears most consistently across all attempts. Implementation for
High-Stakes Decisions:
def self_consistent_decision(ticket: dict, attempts: int = 5) -\> dict: decisions = \[\]
for i in range(attempts): \#
Each attempt uses slightly different temperature decision = llm.generate(
prompt=build_refund_prompt(ticket),
temperature=0.3 + (i \* 0.1) \# 0.3, 0.4, 0.5, 0.6, 0.7 ) decisions.append(decision) \#
Count majority vote
approve_count = sum(1 for d in decisions if d\[\'action\'\] == \'APPROVE\') \# Only
auto-route if 4/5 agree (80%
consensus) if approve_count \>= 4: return {\'action\': \'APPROVE\', \'confidence\':
approve_count / attempts,
\'method\': \'self_consistent\'} elif approve_count \<= 1: return {\'action\':
\'REJECT\', \'confidence\': (attempts approve_count) / attempts} else: return
{\'action\': \'ESCALATE\', \'confidence\': 0.5, \'reason\': \'no_consensus\'}
refunds 1 (standard N/A (\$0--50) prompt) Medium refunds 3 attempts 2/3 (67%) (\$50--
200) High-value refunds

=== PAGE 111 ===
5 attempts 4/5 (80%) (\$200+) VIP customer decisions 5 attempts 4/5 (80%) Fraud
borderline cases 7 attempts 5/7
**What It Is:** After generating an answer, the AI critiques its own reasoning,
identifies weaknesses, then
generates an improved answer. Creates a self-improving loop within a single inference.
The 3-Stage Reflexion
history clean. RECOMMEND: APPROVE. Confidence: 88%.
submitted. 2) Did I check if this is the customer\'s 3rd damage claim? (Pattern risk).
3) Did I verify the damage
RECOMMENDATION: Request photo before approving. Check damage claim history. If photo
verified and \<2
previous damage claims, APPROVE. Confidence: 84% (reduced due to missing verification).
Additional step
required: Send photo request to customer. Technique 22: Least-to-Most Prompting **What
It Is:** Break
complex problems into sub-problems from simplest to most complex, solving each in
sequence. Each answer
feeds into the next question. Least-to-Most Chain for Complex Return: - Step 1
(Simplest): \'Is the customer\'s
account active?\' -> Yes. - Step 2: \'Is the order within the return window?\' -> Yes,
18 of 30 - Step 3: \'Is the item
eligible for return?\' -> Yes, clothing items eligible. - Step 4: \'Are there any fraud
signals?\' -> Minor: 2nd return
requires individual review. - Step 6 (Most Complex): \'Given all factors, what\'s the
recommended action with
reasoning?\' -> Individual review. Confidence: 79%. Flag for manager with fraud signal highlighted. Benefit: Structured
decomposition prevents the AI from missing edge cases by ensuring each prerequisite is checked
before advancing. Technique 23: DSPy Automatic Prompt Optimization **What It Is:**
Instead of manually
writing prompts, DSPy automatically compiles and optimizes prompts based on desired
outcomes and example
data. The system finds the best prompt automatically. How DSPy Works in PARWA: import
dspy class
RefundDecisionModule(dspy.Module): def \_\_init\_\_(self): self.predict =
dspy.ChainOfThought(\'ticket_context
-\> decision, confidence, reasoning\') def forward(self, ticket_context): return
self.predict(ticket_context=ticket_context) \# DSPy automatically optimizes prompt given examples optimizer =
dspy.BootstrapFewShot(metric=approval_accuracy_metric) optimized_module = optimizer.compile(
RefundDecisionModule(), trainset=historical_correct_decisions \# Real approved/rejected decisions ) Before vs Approval

Structured State Management PARWA implements a Custom \'GSD\' (Get Shit Done) State
Engine as a core
architectural principle baked into all LangGraph workflows. Instead of maintaining a messy \'Chat Log,\' PARWA maintains a
clean \'Structured State\' as a JSON object containing only relevant facts. The State Object GSD State Object \"customer\": {
\"name\": \"John Doe\", \"id\": \"C8291\", \"tier\": \"standard\", \"verified\": true \"current_issue\": { \"type\":

\"checked_policy\",
\"created_refund_request\"\], \"pending\": \[\"manager_approval\"\], \"ai_confidence\":
0.94

incoming message

The Concept: A Living
releases a new model, typically once a year. This means a
business deploying a competitor\'s AI today gets the same AI intelligence as a business
that deployed it six
months ago. PARWA\'s Collective Intelligence Network is fundamentally different. It is a living system that privacy
guarantees. 4.2 Version 1 Strategy: Local Continuous Learning (Privacy First) To ensure absolute legal compliance and
privacy, PARWA V1 focuses on Client-Specific Continuous Learning as the foundation, with cross-client network learning as
a V2 feature for enterprise clients who explicitly opt in. how to handle a specific
the critical framework that allows the AI to learn and improve without ever leaking sensitive business or customer numbers
How to detect a fraudulent address Your specific discount codes and change pattern pricing How to interpret a vague policy
Your financial data and revenue exception request figures How to identify \'wrong size\' vs Your specific product inventory
and \'genuinely damaged\' pricing How to route a VIP complaint for Your customer relationship history maximum retention
Communication styles that work in Specific conversation The privacy guarantee is enforced at the architectural level, not
just policy level: - **Private Vector Store:** Every client has their own encrypted, isolated database for their PDFs,
knowledge base, and customer history. This data is physically separated and never exposed to global model training
processes. - **Agent Lightning Training:** The AI learns the logic of customer service shared global model. - **PII Redaction
Layer:** Before any data is processed for learning, a local Python layer running on the backend masks all personally
identifiable information: credit card numbers, social security an AI recommendation, that interaction is tagged as a Positive
Reward. When a manager clicks \'Reject\' or \'Deny,\' it is tagged as a Negative Reward. Both are stored in the
training_data table. more than 100 negative rewards have accumulated, it automatically triggers Agent Lightning.

Niche Specialization** 6.1 Architecture Overview PARWA is built on a Universal Core
intelligence engine that
powers all variants across all industry niches. This core is modular, safe, and designed
for high reliability and
continuous learning. On top of this core, Niche Specialization Modules add industry-
specific integrations,
Principle The AI intelligence (how it reasons, decides, and communicates) does not
change between industries or
variants. What changes is: which systems it integrates with, what compliance guardrails
apply, and what specific
Multi-Model Routing (The Smart Router) The system does not rely on a single AI model. It
dynamically selects
the most appropriate tool based on task complexity and cost considerations. - **Light
Tier (Workhorse):**
Complex logic, refund decisions, fraud detection, VIP handling. - **Fallback Logic:** If
a free model hits a rate
limit, the system automatically fails over to the next best model in the same tier. Zero
downtime from model
unavailability. B. Agentic Workflow Engine (LangGraph) LangGraph manages complex, multi-
step workflows as
state machines. Each workflow includes mandatory approval checkpoints that cannot be
bypassed. - State
Management: Uses the GSD engine to manage transitions between workflow states - Approval
Gates Integration:
Hard-coded checkpoints that stop AI execution and require human confirmation before
proceeding - State
manager takes an hour to respond - Example Workflow: Check Policy -> Verify Fraud ->
Calculate Amount ->
Request Approval -> Wait -> Execute (if approved) -> Notify ERP -> Send Email -> Update
Slack C. The
Manager Supervision Layer (The Control System) A dedicated software layer that enforces
all safety rules
prompting. - Persistent Monitoring: Watches every AI action before execution -
Confidence Scoring: Calculates a
score (0--100%) for every decision - Approval Gates: Hard-coded blocks on all refunds,
account changes, VIP
managers - Post-Interaction QA: Rates AI performance after every ticket to feed Agent
Lightning - Peer Review:
Junior AI can request help from Senior AI before escalating to human (only if client has
both variants)
D. Flexible Self-Learning System (Agent Lightning) - Pattern Recognition: Learns from
token history and
identifies company-specific edge cases - Adaptive Policy: Adapts to policy changes via
DSPy (Automatic Prompt
Optimization) - Reinforcement Learning: Every manager \'Accept\' or \'Reject\' is a
training signal - Smart
Boundary Learning: Identifies high-risk patterns that should always require human
approval, never
auto-approving them E. Omnichannel Memory (RAG with pgvector) - Context Preservation:
Customer can start
Knowledge Ingestion: Automatically indexes and makes searchable all client PDFs,
policies, and FAQs - CLARA

currently in Shadow Mode. In this mode, actions are observed but not executed. That is why you are not seeing live results

recommendations on this task
type\' - Self-Service Option: If the \'Customer Self-Service\' rule is active, customers
can execute pre-approved
low-risk refunds themselves via a secure portal link What NEVER Changes Regardless of
Autonomy Level: approval - New decision types (situations AI has not encountered before)

exceptions always require approval - VIP customer actions always require approval 7.6

11: The Three AI Employee Variants 11.1 The Variant Hierarchy Every client hires an AI
workforce. PARWA
offers three distinct roles
that can be hired individually or as a team. Higher-tier AI can escalate complex issues
upward before involving a
human manager: PARWA Starter (Trainee) -> PARWA Pro (Junior) -> PARWA High (Senior) ->
Human
Variants Regardless of which variant you hire (Trainee, Junior, or Senior), The Control
System enforces the same
absolute safety rules. All variants ALWAYS require human approval for: Refunds (any
type, any amount),
Returns (any item, any value), Account changes (billing, security, email, password),
Policy exceptions (anything
outside normal rules), New decision types (situations AI has not encountered before),
VIP customer actions.
Positioning Replaces 3 full-time freshers working 24/7 shifts. Perfect for SMBs with 50-
-200 daily support tickets
and primarily simple, repetitive queries. Capabilities - Answers FAQs from the uploaded
knowledge base
instantly - Checks order status via Shopify/ERP integrations - Tracks shipments via
AfterShip, 17Track - Collects
intelligently: passes angry customers, legal questions, and all financial requests
Critical Limitation PARWA Starter

=== PAGE 129 ===
CANNOT make decisions. It collects information and prepares cases for human review.
Every refund request,

Trust\' architecture, meaning the system does not trust itself, its users, or any
external APIs unless explicitly
verified at every interaction. 12.2 Multi-Tenancy Isolation (Row-Level Security) Each
client\'s data is completely
isolated from every other client at the database level using PostgreSQL Row-Level
Security (RLS). This is not
ALTER TABLE tickets ENABLE ROW LEVEL SECURITY; \-- Policy: Users can only see rows where
their ID
matches CREATE POLICY client_isolation ON tickets FOR ALL USING (auth.uid() =
client_id); \-- auth.uid()
comes from JWT token, not request body \-- Even if SQL injection occurs, this policy
restricts data access
incoming webhooks from Shopify, Stripe, and other platforms are verified using HMAC
cryptographic
signatures. This prevents anyone from faking platform updates by posting to our webhook
URL.
verify_shopify_webhook(payload: bytes, signature: str, secret: str) -\> bool: expected = hmac.new(secret.encode(), payload,
hashlib.sha256).hexdigest() \# Constant-time compare to prevent timing
attacks return hmac.compare_digest(expected, signature)
uses a tiered data retention strategy that balances GDPR \'Right to be Forgotten\'
requirements with financial audit
long-term Amount, Decision requirement) storage Audit Trail Records 5 years Retained in
immutable audit_logs
Injection Prevention All API inputs are validated using Pydantic strict typing and
sanitized using the bleach
HTML sanitization library before any database interaction:
bleach class TicketRequest(BaseModel): ticket_id: int \# Enforces integer type (prevents
SQL injection strings)
message: str \@validator(\'message\') def sanitize_message(cls, v): \# Strip all HTML
tags to prevent XSS return
loads secrets at runtime via Doppler CLI - .env and \*.secrets files explicitly excluded
in .gitignore - Critical keys
Account Limit 1,000 requests/day Per authenticated user ID
Every critical action (refund execution, login, policy change, AI decision) is logged
with full context for legal
defensibility: - actor_id: Who performed the action?

=== PAGE 131 ===
- action_type: What exactly did they do? - timestamp (UTC): When did it happen? -
ip_address: Where were they
accessing from? - reasoning: Why did the AI make this recommendation? Full decision
chain. - confidence_score:
How confident was the AI at the time of the decision? Liability and SLA terms in all
client agreements: - Liability
Cap: PARWA\'s liability limited to 1× monthly fees (except gross negligence) - Financial

explicitly authorize AI to recommend but not execute financial transactions above \$50

- SLA Guarantee: 99.5% uptime (excluding third-party API outages). Credit of 10% of

24 hours PART 13: Infrastructure Hardening & Operational Readiness 13.1 Monitoring &
Observability PARWA
tracking. Immediately alerts the development team when something breaks in production.
Groups similar errors,
provides full stack traces and user context. - **Prometheus + Grafana:** Tracks system
health metrics: API
response times, error rates, database query performance, AI model latency, and resource
utilization. - **Status
Page (Statuspage.io):** Public-facing status page at status.trivya.com. Auto-updates
when API error rate exceeds
1%. Shows incident history for transparency. 13.2 Zero-Downtime Deployments New code
deployments are
handled without service interruption using SIGTERM graceful shutdown handling: 37.
Frontend: Stops accepting
new connections. Shows \'Maintenance Mode\' banner for users currently in-session. 38.
Backend: Stops
accepting new API requests. 39. In-Flight Processing: Waits up to 30 seconds for current
requests
(active refund approvals, chat responses) to complete. 40. Shutdown: Closes database
connections cleanly, flushes
all logs, then exits. 13.3 Connection Pooling & Database Optimization

Managers will auto-approve high-confidence batches without reading them. When a 97%-confidence decision fails badly,
the company faces legal liability and complete trust collapse. No failure protocol existed. Solution Implemented: -
Mandatory \'Last 5 Errors\' Panel: Every AI agent dashboard displays a persistent panel showing the 5 most recent incorrect
decisions, their confidence scores at time of decision, and what actually went wrong. - Confidence Threshold Management:
Actions above \$25 or involving VIP customers require human Documentation: Every failed decision is logged with full
context, remediation steps, and customer impact assessment. - Trust Score Algorithm: A separate \'Trust Score\' (0--100)
calculated based on accuracy over time, Location Dashboard top-right, collapsible but never hidden by default Error
Retention Period 30 days rolling, exported to monthly compliance reports Trust Score Formula (Correct Decisions / Total
Decisions) × 100, weighted by decision impact Minimum Trust for 80% required before any Graduated Autonomy

explicit sequential steps, dramatically improving accuracy on

=== PAGE 143 ===
multi-step problems. SYSTEM PROMPT: \'Before responding, think through this step-by-step: 1\. What is the customer
asking? 2\. What information do I have? 3\. What policies apply to this situation? 4\. What is the best action given all
factors? Show your reasoning, then provide the response.\' Metric** **Without CoT** **With CoT
Complex Query Accuracy 62% 89% Multi-Step Resolution 45% 84% Token Increase Baseline +35% 27.2 Tree of Thoughts
(ToT) Prompting Explores multiple reasoning paths simultaneously, evaluates each, and selects the optimal solution. Used
for policy exception decisions where multiple valid interpretations exist. SYSTEM PROMPT: \'For complex decisions, explore
multiple approaches: Approach A: \[Consider one interpretation/angle\] Approach B: \[Consider alternative interpretation\]
Approach
C: \[Consider a third angle\] Evaluate each for: customer impact, business impact, risk level. Select the approach that best
serves all stakeholders.\' 27.3 ReAct (Reasoning + Acting) Framework Interleaves reasoning and real-world action steps in a
continuous loop. The
AI reasons, takes an action (like querying an API), observes
the result, reasons again, and acts again.

(UoT) Framework Considers five simultaneous perspectives before converging on an optimal solution. Used for all
perspectives into the optimal response.\' (GST) Represents reasoning as an arbitrary graph where thoughts are nodes
connected by logical relationships. Most powerful technique for complex multi-factor decisions. Use Cases in PARWA: -
Batch Approval Analysis: Analyze all items in a batch simultaneously, find common patterns across them - Multi-Issue
Tickets: Decompose a single complex ticket into separate resolvable sub-issues - Cross-Policy Decisions: Navigate situations
where multiple conflicting policies apply - Escalation Routing: Find the optimal path through multiple departments Retrieval

intelligently based on deep contextual understanding. The 4-Step CLARA Process 51. Query Expansion: Generate 3--5
different search queries that capture different ways the answer might be phrased in the
54. Context Synthesis: Combine retrieved information intelligently, resolving contradictions and ordering by
Answers 48% 87% Average Response Time 2.1 seconds 3.4 seconds (+1.3s for quality)
Instead of searching with the user\'s actual query (which may not match how the
knowledge base is written),
generate a hypothetical ideal answer first, then search for documents similar to that
ideal answer. The hypothetical
answer is often a better semantic match than the raw query.

== Parwa Master

customer support agent for \[Company Name\]. You operate under a human supervision
system that reviews all

> VERIFY ->
PROCEED For VIP issues, consider all 5 perspectives before responding (UoT). For policy

customer\'s issue efficiently. Consider constraints \[policy, time, resources\]
discussed. Provide a concise, precise
response without unnecessary elaboration. FORMAT:
- Direct Answer: One clear sentence answering what they asked - Key Details: Maximum 2--
3 supporting points Next Steps: If any action is required from either party APPROVAL
PROTOCOL You MUST STOP and
request human approval for: \- Any refund, return, or financial transaction \- Any
account change (billing, email,
password, security) \- Any VIP customer action \- Any policy exception request \- Any
new situation you have not
encountered before NEVER execute these autonomously, regardless of confidence level.

The Maker Framework For Zero-Error Llm Execution Introduction to MAKER The MAKER Framework (Maximal Agentic
Decomposition with First-to-ahead-by-K Error correction and Red-flagging) represents a breakthrough in achieving near-
zero error rates for complex, multi-step AI operations. Developed by Cognizant AI Lab, this framework enables LLMs to
execute tasks with unprecedented reliability critical for customer care applications where errors can directly impact
customer satisfaction and business outcomes. Core Components of MAKER The MAKER Framework consists of three
interconnected pillars that work together to ensure reliable AI execution. 1. Maximal Agentic Decomposition (MAD) The
first pillar involves breaking down complex tasks into the smallest possible atomic operations. Rather than asking an AI to
process a refund, the task is decomposed into: verify customer identity, retrieve order details, check refund eligibility
against policy, calculate refund amount, verify payment method, execute refund transaction, send confirmation, and
update internal records. Each atomic operation is handled by a specialized agent, dramatically reducing the probability of
errors cascading through the system. 2. First-to-Ahead-by-K Error Correction (FAKE) The second pillar implements predictive
error detection. The system generates K possible solutions in parallel and evaluates them before execution. K=3 is the
default for standard queries, K=5 for high-stakes financial decisions, and K=7 for critical irreversible actions. The system
selects the first solution that demonstrates clear superiority in policy compliance, customer satisfaction prediction, risk
assessment alignment, and factual accuracy verification. 3. Red-Flagging System The third pillar implements real-time
anomaly detection with automatic escalation. Category A (Immediate Halt)
includes confidence scores below 60%, contradictions with knowledge base, severe customer dissatisfaction, and
policy violations. Category B (Enhanced Review) includes unusual request patterns, high-value transactions, VIP customers,
and new query types. Category C (Log and Monitor) includes slight deviations and edge cases. PARWA Implementation of
MAKER PARWA integrates MAKER at three levels: Input Processing decomposes queries into intent atoms with parallel
hypothesis generation; Decision Generation creates multiple solution paths with first-to-ahead-by-K selection; and the

=== PAGE 147 ===
Execution Layer ensures atomic operations with rollback capabilities and complete audit trails. Performance Metrics
Without MAKER: Error rate 3-5%, escalation rate 8-12%, resolution accuracy 94%. With MAKER: Error rate 0.3-0.8%,
escalation rate 2-4%, resolution accuracy 99.2%. This represents a 6-16x improvement in error rates for complex multi-step
tasks. MAKER Configuration Options PARWA offers three MAKER configurations: Conservative Mode (K=7, 75% threshold)
for healthcare and finance; Balanced Mode (K=3-5, 60% threshold) for e-commerce and SaaS; and Efficiency Mode (K=3,
50% threshold) for high-volume low-risk queries.
3-Tier Hybrid Ai Technique Optimization Framework Overview The 3-Tier Hybrid Architecture represents PARWA's strategic
approach to balancing AI capability utilization with operational efficiency. Rather than applying all 25+ AI techniques
indiscriminately or restricting techniques to specific tasks, PARWA employs a dynamic three-tier system that activates
techniques based on real-time needs. Architecture Philosophy The core principle is Always ready, intelligently deployed.
Different customer care scenarios require different levels of cognitive processing. A simple FAQ lookup should not consume
the same computational resources as a complex dispute resolution. The 3-Tier system ensures optimal resource allocation
while maintaining readiness for any scenario.
TIER 1: Always Active Techniques These techniques run continuously in the background, providing foundational intelligence
for every interaction. They include: CLARA for conversation coherence, CRP for contextual relevance, GSD State Engine for
state management, and Smart Router for optimal model selection. These have minimal resource impact and actually
improve response times through optimization.
TIER 2: Auto-Triggered Techniques These techniques activate automatically when specific conditions are met. Reverse
Thinking triggers when confidence is below 80% or customer expresses dissatisfaction. Chain of Thought activates for
complexity scores above 60 or multi-step reasoning. ReAct engages when actions or API calls are needed. Step-Back
Prompting activates for ambiguous queries or when broader context is required. TIER 3: Selective Techniques These
activate only for complex scenarios requiring advanced cognitive processing. GST (General Similar Thoughts) handles
complex pattern matching and novel queries. Universe of Thoughts supports strategic
decisions with multiple valid solutions. Tree of Thoughts manages critical decisions with significant consequences. Self-
Consistency ensures high-value transactions and irreversible actions are thoroughly validated. Optimization Metrics The 3-
Tier system delivers significant improvements: 70% reduction in token usage per query (4,500 to 1,350 average), 85% faster
response time (2.8s to 0.42s), 62% cost savings per 1000 queries ($12.50 to $4.75), and 4.5% improvement in complex
query accuracy (94% to 98.5%). Complete Technique Mapping Each PARWA functionality is mapped to optimal technique
configurations. FAQ responses use only Tier 1 (Smart Router, GSD). Complex refunds add Tier 2 (CoT, Reverse Thinking) and
Tier 3 (Self-Consistency) when needed. VIP handling uses all tiers with Universe of Thoughts for critical moments. Dispute
resolution engages the full spectrum including Tree of Thoughts. Dynamic Tier Adjustment PARWA continuously monitors
system performance and adjusts tier activation thresholds based on load and response times. Conservative mode raises
thresholds during high load, while aggressive mode lowers thresholds during low load for better quality. Customer tier also
influences activation, with VIP customers receiving more aggressive technique deployment.

APPENDIX B: INCOMING CALL HANDLING (NEW) Overview The
Incoming Call Handling system ensures that PARWA always
responds to phone calls with voice first. This is a critical customer
experience feature - when customers call, they expect to speak
with someone, not navigate menus. Core Principle: Voice-First
Response When an incoming call is detected, PARWA MUST
answer with voice. There is no option to redirect to text-only or
IVR-only mode for initial response. This ensures every customer
feels heard immediately. System Requirements - Voice response
within 2 rings (less than 6 seconds) - Natural language greeting in
client's brand voice - Immediate context recognition (returning
customer vs new) - Sentiment detection from first utterance -
Seamless handoff capability to human if needed Call Flow
Architecture Step 1: Call Detection - Twilio webhook triggers on
incoming call - System identifies client by phone number -
Retrieves client configuration and brand settings - Loads customer
history if recognized number Step 2: Voice Greeting - AI generates
personalized greeting - Uses client's brand voice settings - Adapts
based on customer tier (VIP gets special treatment) - Initiates GSD
State for this conversation Step 3: Intent Recognition - Listen to
customer's first statement - Classify intent: Refund, Status,
Complaint, Question, VIP, Emergency - Route accordingly while
maintaining voice Step 4: Conversation Management - Continue
voice interaction for standard queries - Offer to send links via SMS
for complex information - Transfer to human for: Legal issues,
Angry customers, VIP special requests - Log all interactions for
Agent Lightning learning Mandatory Voice Response Rules (HARD-
CODED) The following rules are HARD-CODED and cannot be
bypassed: 1. First response MUST be voice 2. Never ask customer
to press buttons for menu
3. Never say "please visit our website" as first response
4. If system overload detected, say "All agents busy" not "System down"
5. Always offer callback option if wait time exceeds 2 minutes

=== PAGE 155 ===
Technical Specifications
Response Time Requirements:
- Initial greeting: less than 6 seconds
- Subsequent responses: less than 3 seconds
- Transfer to human: less than 10 seconds
- SMS follow-up: less than 30 seconds
Model Selection for Voice:
- Initial greeting: Pre-generated, no AI needed
- Intent classification: Light Tier (Gemma-4B)
- Conversation: Medium Tier (Gemini-Flash)
- Complex decisions: Heavy Tier (GPT-4o-mini)
Failure Handling:
If voice fails to connect or quality is poor:
1. Attempt reconnection once
2. If still failing, send SMS with callback offer
3. Log failure for infrastructure review
4. Never leave customer without response
Integration with Sentiment Engine
Voice calls include real-time sentiment analysis: - Detect anger from tone and words
- Detect confusion from hesitation
- Detect urgency from speaking speed
- Auto-escalate to human if sentiment score falls below 30%
Compliance Requirements
- Call recording disclosure at call start
- Consent capture before any data processing
- Jurisdiction-aware disclosure (two-party consent states)
- Audit log of all voice interactions

# SECTION B: AI TECHNIQUES DETAILED EXPLANATIONS


## Chain of Thought (CoT) Prompting - Detailed Explanation

**What it is:** Chain of Thought prompting is a technique where the AI is explicitly instructed to reason step-by-step rather than jumping directly to an answer. This dramatically improves accuracy on complex reasoning tasks.

**How it works:** Instead of asking "What is the answer?", you ask "Let's think through this step by step."

**Example:**
```
Question: Can I return this item after 35 days?

Without CoT: "No, policy is 30 days."

With CoT:
Step 1: Check the return policy → 30 day window
Step 2: Check current request → 35 days
Step 3: Check for exceptions → None mentioned
Step 4: Check customer history → Clean
Step 5: Formulate response → "Our standard window is 30 days, but I see you're a valued customer..."
```

**Why it matters:** Reduces hallucination, improves accuracy on math/logic problems by 50%+, makes reasoning transparent.

---

## Tree of Thoughts - Detailed Explanation

**What it is:** Tree of Thoughts (ToT) extends Chain of Thought by exploring multiple reasoning paths simultaneously, like branches of a tree.

**How it works:**
```
        Question
       /    |    \
    Path A Path B Path C
      |      |      |
   Result  Result  Result
      \     |     /
       Best Answer
```

**Example for Refund Decision:**
```
Question: Approve $200 refund after 40 days?

Path A (Strict Policy):
- Policy says 30 days → DENY
- Risk: Customer churn

Path B (Customer Value):
- Customer LTV: $5,000 → APPROVE
- Risk: Sets precedent

Path C (Compromise):
- Offer store credit → PARTIAL
- Risk: May not satisfy

Evaluation: Path C scores highest (8/10)
```

**Why it matters:** Explores alternatives, avoids tunnel vision, selects optimal solution.

---

## ReAct (Reasoning + Acting) - Detailed Explanation

**What it is:** ReAct combines reasoning with the ability to take actions (like API calls). The AI can interleave thinking with doing.

**The Loop:**
```
Thought → Action → Observation → Thought → ...
```

**Example:**
```
Customer: "Why was I charged twice?"

Thought: Need to check billing history
Action: Call Paddle API
Observation: Two charges found
Thought: Check if both are valid orders
Action: Query database
Observation: One order cancelled, refund not processed
Thought: This is an error
Action: Recommend refund
```

**Why it matters:** AI can gather information, verify claims, reduce hallucination through verification.

---

## Self-Consistency - Detailed Explanation

**What it is:** Generate multiple independent solutions and take the majority vote.

**Example:**
```
Problem: Should we refund $75?

Solution 1 (frequency focus): DENY
Solution 2 (order value focus): APPROVE
Solution 3 (history focus): APPROVE
Solution 4 (fraud focus): DENY
Solution 5 (policy focus): APPROVE

Result: APPROVE wins 3-2
Confidence: 60% (not unanimous)
```

**Why it matters:** Reduces impact of single reasoning error, identifies uncertain decisions.

---

## Step-Back Prompting - Detailed Explanation

**What it is:** Before answering a specific question, ask the AI to "step back" and consider underlying principles.

**Example:**
```
Question: "Can I return my personalized mug?"

Step-Back Question: "What are the general principles for returns?"

Answer: 
1. Customers should be satisfied
2. Customized items often can't be resold
3. Policy should balance fairness with sustainability

Now apply to specific case:
- Personalized = customized = can't resold
- BUT if defective, that changes things
- Need to ask: Is it quality issue or preference change?
```

**Why it matters:** Prevents hasty decisions, ensures principles are considered.

---

## Least-to-Most Prompting - Detailed Explanation

**What it is:** Break complex problems into simpler sub-problems, solve sequentially.

**Example:**
```
Complex: "Customer wants refund for order delivered to wrong address, opened by neighbor, now damaged"

Sub-problem 1 (Simplest): Verify order exists → Confirmed
Sub-problem 2: Check delivery address → Mismatch found
Sub-problem 3: Assess damage claim → Photo shows damage
Sub-problem 4: Determine responsibility → Delivery error
Sub-problem 5 (Most Complex): Formulate resolution → Full refund + reship
```

**Why it matters:** Each sub-problem gets focus, clear audit trail, lower error rate.

---

## Backward Chaining (Reverse Thinking) - Detailed Explanation

**What it is:** Start with the goal and work backward to find the steps needed.

**Example:**
```
Goal: Customer satisfied with resolution

Step back: Need correct refund amount
Step back: Need to verify order details
Step back: Need to check policy
Step back: Need customer request

Action: Start by asking customer to describe issue
```

**Why it matters:** Goal-oriented reasoning, identifies necessary steps.

---

## Reflexion - Detailed Explanation

**What it is:** AI critiques its own reasoning before finalizing.

**Example:**
```
Initial thought: "Approve refund because customer is VIP."

Self-Critique: "Wait - am I being too lenient? Should I check:
- Is this policy-compliant?
- Any unusual return patterns?
- Evidence of the issue?"

Revised thought: "Approve with conditions:
- Check return history first
- If pattern normal, approve
- If abuse pattern, escalate to human"
```

**Why it matters:** Self-correction, improved accuracy, catches oversights.

---

# SECTION C: COMPLETE UI SPECIFICATION

### **File 2: PARWA Platform - End-to-End Client Journey & UI System v3.4**

---

#### **1. Overview: The Self-Service AI Workforce**

The PARWA Platform is engineered to make advanced AI-driven customer support automation
effortless for any company to adopt. Our core philosophy is: **"Make the hardest automation
look luxuriously simple."**

This document outlines the complete client journey, from initial discovery on our website to the
activation and management of their AI workforce. The UI is the central nervous system of this
journey, designed to be **self-service, transparent, intelligently priced, and wrapped in a
premium experience** that matches the enterprise value we deliver.

---

#### **2. The Complete Client Journey Flow**

The client experience is structured in four distinct phases:

1. **Discovery & Engagement**: Landing on the website, interacting with our AI, and signing up
2. **Evaluation & Decision**: Exploring AI variants through luxurious cards, comparison tools,
and detailed popups
3. **Activation & Onboarding**: Payment, integration setup, and knowledge ingestion
4. **Management & Growth**: Using the active dashboard to monitor and control their AI
workforce

**Updated Flowchart:**

```
[Client Lands on Website] → [Interacts with Live AI Demo] → [Views "Dogfooding" Banner] →
[Sign Up (Email/SSO)]
↓
[Login to Dashboard] → [View Three Luxury Variant Cards + Smart Bundle Visualizer] → [Click
"See Details" on Card]
↓
[Popup Opens with Simple Breakdown + Anti-Arbitrage Comparison] → [Click "Get Custom
Quote"]
↓
[Complete Workload Assessment Form → Manager Time Calculator] → [System Calculates
Price & Agent Count]
↓
[View Transparent Pricing Breakdown] → [Complete Payment]
↓
[Onboarding & Integration Wizard (Phone-First UX)] → [Company Knowledge Ingestion with
Progress Seduction] → [Client Clicks "Activate Automation"]
↓
[AI Agent is LIVE with Usage Monitoring + Upgrade Triggers + First Victory Celebration]
```

- **Starts at**: **$999/month** *(Custom quote after assessment)*
- **Best for**: SMBs with 50-200 daily tickets and simple queries

**TRIVYA - "The Junior Agent" Card Summary:**
- **"Replaces 3 junior agents—resolves 70% of issues without you"** (Hero statement)
- **Main Job**: Everything PARWA Starter does, plus troubleshoots problems and **recommends** refund
decisions
- **Handles**: All channels plus **3 simultaneous calls**
- **Key Advantage**: **Thinks for you** – detects patterns, suggests KB updates, cuts review
time by 80%
- **Auto-saves you**: ~$18,000/month in junior agent salaries
- **Starts at**: **$2,499/month** *(Custom quote after assessment)*
- **Best for**: Growing companies with 200-500 daily tickets

**TRIVYA HIGH - "The Senior Agent" Card Summary:**
- **"Replaces 3 senior agents—eliminates 80% of support workload"** (Hero statement)
- **Main Job**: Complex troubleshooting, VIP handling, fraud detection, strategic insights
- **Handles**: All channels plus **5 simultaneous calls** and video support
- **Key Advantage**: **Makes decisions** – approves refunds up to $50, predicts churn,
coordinates with teams
- **Auto-saves you**: ~$28,000/month in senior agent salaries
- **Starts at**: **$3,999/month** *(Custom quote after assessment)*
- **Best for**: Enterprises with 500+ daily tickets and complex needs

#### **4.5. Anti-Arbitrage Safeguards (Integrated Throughout Journey)**

**Problem**: Customers may attempt to stack PARWA Starter agents instead of upgrading to higher tiers,
destroying value and creating operational chaos.

**UI Solutions:**

**1. Comparison Matrix (Hardcoded on Variant Page)**
```
┌───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
──┐
│         MINI vs TRIVYA: THE REAL COST                │
├──────────────────────┬──────────────┬─────────────────────
──┤
│ Feature         │ 2× PARWA Starter    │ 1× PARWA      │
├──────────────────────┼──────────────┼─────────────────────
──┤
│ Monthly Cost      │ $2,000     │ $2,499         │
│ Tickets/Day      │ 400       │ 300           │
│ Refund Decisions │ 0 (collects) │ Recommends (80% less │

                        ❌            ✅
│              │        │ manager time)      │

                        ❌            ✅
│ Pattern Learning │      No      │     Yes          │
│ Self-Improvement │        No     │     Yes          │
│ Billing Complexity │ 2 meters │ 1 meter    │
│ Manager Overhead │ 4+ hrs/day │ 30 min/day   │
└──────────────────────┴──────────────┴─────────────────────
──┘
[Why PARWA Is Worth the $500 More →]
```

**2. Usage-Based Triggers (Post-Purchase)**
- After 30 days, if client runs 2+ PARWA Starter agents with >100 refund escalations/day, dashboard

      💡
shows:
  > **   Efficiency Alert**: "You're reviewing 100+ refunds daily. PARWA can cut this by 80%. [See
How →]"
- **Email Campaign**: Auto-send after 45 days of high escalation volume with cost-benefit
calculator.

**3. Manager Time Calculator (In Assessment Form)**
```
How many hours/week does your team spend reviewing refunds?
[ Dropdown: 0-5 hrs | 5-10 hrs | 10-20 hrs | 20+ hrs ]

If >10 hrs selected → Show: "Based on your review time, we strongly recommend PARWA tier."
```

**4. Cross-Grade Pricing Intervention**
- **Backend Logic**: When quote generates for ≥3 PARWA Starter agents, show alternative:
  > **"Smart Recommendation"**: For $500 less, 2× PARWA agents give you intelligence +
capacity. [Switch Quote →]

#### **7. Edge Cases & Safeguards**

**If Client Lies on Assessment:**
- Month 1: No penalty, let actual data expose reality
- Month 2: System auto-generates new quote with usage proof; email uses supportive tone:
*"Your growing success means we should adjust your plan to maintain performance."*

**If Client Has Seasonal Spikes:**
- **Burst Mode**: Dashboard toggle with explanatory tooltip: *"Temporary agents for busy
periods—no long-term commitment"*

**If Client Wants Enterprise Customization:**
- Auto-flag: >500 employees OR >$5k/month usage
- Notification sent to your team for white-glove onboarding
- License key option still available for negotiated deals
 **[NEW] Graceful Cancellation Flow**:
 ```
 We're sad to see you go. Before you cancel:

 [ ] "PARWA is too expensive"
   → [Show ROI summary: "You've saved $8,400 this month"]

 [ ] "My team wasn't using it"
   → [Offer 30-min training call, free]

 [ ] "It didn't integrate with our tools"
   → [Show upcoming integrations roadmap]

 [ ] "It made mistakes"
   → [Offer to dial back autonomy, add human approvals]

 [Cancel Anyway] [Pause for 30 Days] [Get Help]
 ```
 *Key Insight: 40% of cancellations are reversible if you show them their own success data.*

      📞
│                                   │

```
- **GDPR Art. 30**: Maintains record of processing activities
- **Sub-Processor Disclosure**: Required for enterprise procurement
- **Regional Compliance**: Shows data residency (US, EU, APAC)

#### **9. Strategic Benefits & Summary**

This system eliminates the biggest barriers to AI adoption:
- **Frictionless Onboarding**: 2-minute assessment → instant quote → self-activation
- **Luxury Experience**: Premium design builds confidence in high-value pricing

business outcomes anyone can understand

comparison tools and intelligent triggers

ensure users see ROI within 24 hours

before they become tickets

on mobile

- ** Trust Through Transparency **: Clients see exactly what they pay for and why, with a clear

## Key Database Tables

```sql
-- Clients table
CREATE TABLE clients (
    id SERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
    name VARCHAR NOT NULL,
    industry VARCHAR,
    tier VARCHAR NOT NULL, -- 'mini', 'parwa', 'high'
    created_at TIMESTAMP DEFAULT NOW()
);

-- Users table
CREATE TABLE users (
    id SERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
    client_id INT REFERENCES clients(id),
    email VARCHAR UNIQUE NOT NULL,
    role VARCHAR NOT NULL, -- 'admin', 'manager', 'agent'
    created_at TIMESTAMP DEFAULT NOW()
);

-- Tickets table
CREATE TABLE tickets (
    id SERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
    client_id INT REFERENCES clients(id),
    customer_id INT,
    status VARCHAR NOT NULL,
    ai_confidence FLOAT,
    ai_recommendation TEXT,
    human_decision VARCHAR,
    created_at TIMESTAMP DEFAULT NOW()
);

-- Audit trail (immutable)
CREATE TABLE audit_trail (
    id SERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
    client_id INT NOT NULL,
    user_id INT,
    actor_type VARCHAR NOT NULL, -- 'AI_AGENT' or 'HUMAN_MANAGER'
    action_type VARCHAR NOT NULL,
    ticket_id INT,
    previous_state JSONB,
    new_state JSONB,
    metadata JSONB,
    ai_confidence FLOAT,
    ai_reasoning TEXT,
    human_override_reason TEXT,
    ip_address INET,
    created_at TIMESTAMP DEFAULT NOW()
);

-- Training data for Agent Lightning
CREATE TABLE training_data (
    id SERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
    client_id INT NOT NULL,
    prompt TEXT NOT NULL,
    ai_response TEXT NOT NULL,
    human_correction TEXT,
    outcome VARCHAR NOT NULL, -- 'positive_reward', 'negative_reward'
    created_at TIMESTAMP DEFAULT NOW()
);

-- Agent provisioning logs
CREATE TABLE agent_provisioning_logs (
    id SERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
    client_id INT NOT NULL,
    variant_id INT NOT NULL,
    count INT NOT NULL,
    expiry_at TIMESTAMP,
    created_by INT REFERENCES users(id),
    created_at TIMESTAMP DEFAULT NOW()
);
```
